The state estimator must employ Extended Kalman Fiter (EKF) or Unscemed Kalman Fater (UKF) algorithms to deeply fuse data from triaxial gyroscopes. triaxial accelerometers, magnetometers, barometers, GNSS positions and velocities, and pitot-static airspeed sensors. The structural design of the airframe must achieve a precise equilibrium between mechanical rigidity. aerodynamic efficiency. and the empty-weight ratio. For lixed-wing aircraft employing high-aspect-ratio wing geometries, the design of the main spar must prioritize high-modulus carbon fiber composite materials (such as T700 or T800 grade) to guarantee adequate structural torsional stiffness under extreme maneuvering loads (+4 5G to -2.0G). Aerodynamic elasticity and flutter margins must be comprehensively verified through Ground Vibration Testing (GVT), and the actual critical flutter velocity must exceed the maximum design dive speed (Vd) by at least 25% [28] The internal geometric topology of the fuselage must strictly account for Electromagnetic Compatibility (EMC) zoning. High-frequency radio frequency transmitters (such as data link antennas and video transmission modules) must be physically isolated from high-precision analog sensors (such as inertial measurement units iMU and barometers) The airframe shell should incorporate conductive braided mesh or shielding paint at critical junctions to attenuate transient electromagnetic interference generated by power cables during peak current outputs. EXTRACTED TEXT:
Field Evaluation of Wearable Translation Glasses A wearable translation system is most useful when it behaves like an ordinary tool rather than a laboratory demonstration. The user should be able to face a printed page. pause briefly, and hear a clear rendering without holding a telephone or searching through menus. In the prototype described here, a small camera is mounted near eye level and connected to a compact computer Video is sent over a local link to a processing workstation where text detection, optical character recognition, language translation. and speech synthesis are performed. The complete pipeline operates without a cloud service. This arrangement protects sensitive documents. avoids delays caused by an unstable internet connection. and allows every software component to be measured independently Image acquisition is the first major difficulty. A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view The page may be tilted. partly shadowed. or closer at the top than at the bottom Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it It locates groups of text. estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image. and checks that a safe border remains around the detected region Sharpness is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion, because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lines remain soft A frame is accepted only after several consecutive observations agree Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or right, hold still. or improve the lighting After capture, the image is converted to grayscale and corrected only when the correction improves measured recognition. Excessive sharpening can create bright halos around letters. while aggressive thresholding can erase punctuation and thin strokes For that reason. several preprocessing alternatives are tested on the same stored photographs The comparison includes raw grayscale, local contrast enhancement mild gamma correction, edge-preserving filtering. and adaptive binanzation Each alternative is evaluated using character count. recognition confidence, focus statistics, and processing time Ground-truth text is retained for important experiments so that character error rate and word error rate can be calculated instead of relying on confidence alone. The recognition stage preserves reading order and line positions Translation proceeds paragraph by paragraph. while a short tone identifies each new region. Simple controls let the listener repeat the current section or move forward and backward
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The complete pipeline operates without a cloud service. This arrangement protects sensitive documents. avoids delays caused by an unstable internet connection. and allows every software component to be measured independently Image acquisition is the first major difficulty. A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view The page may be tilted. partly shadowed. or closer at the top than at the bottom Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it It locates groups of text. estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image. and checks that a safe border remains around the detected region Sharpness is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion, because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lines remain soft A frame is accepted only after several consecutive observations agree Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or right, hold still. or improve the lighting After capture, the image is converted to grayscale and corrected only when the correction improves measured recognition. Excessive sharpening can create bright halos around letters. while aggressive thresholding can erase punctuation and thin strokes For that reason. several preprocessing alternatives are tested on the same stored photographs The comparison includes raw grayscale, local contrast enhancement mild gamma correction, edge-preserving filtering. and adaptive binanzation Each alternative is evaluated using character count. recognition confidence, focus statistics, and processing time Ground-truth text is retained for important experiments so that character error rate and word error rate can be calculated instead of relying on confidence alone.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

SOURCE     : The recognition stage preserves reading order and line positions Translation proceeds paragraph by paragraph. while a short tone identifies each new region. Simple controls let the listener repeat the current section or move forward and backward

EXTRACTED TEXT:
Autonomous Monitoring of a Remote Hybrid-Energy Station An isolated plateau station powers a medical clinic, radio repeater, weather instruments, and emergency lighting. Its microgrid combines solar paneis. lithium batteries, and a compact diesel generator. Because winter roads may remain closed for days, a local controller samples voltage, current, temperature, and vibration every 200 milliseconds. Detailed records stay on site, while compressed summaries are transmitted whenever the link becomes available. Medical and communications loads always receive priority On 18 October 2025, a dust storm reduced solar generation by 34 percent in fifteen minutes. Battery-cabinet temperature increased by 8 °C, and the inverter fan developed an unusual low-frequency vibration. Rather than shut down the station, the controller disconnected secondary heaters, reduced selected lighting, and started the backup generator. Diagnostic software separated the incident into three likely faults: debris on the solar array, wear in a fan bearing. and rising contact resistance at a battery connector After the storm. a head-mounted camera read equipment labels and alarm codes. which a local processor compared with an offline manual. Sensitive images were not uploaded to the cloud. The capture program required the complete label to remain inside a safe border and checked sharpness across the full frame and its upper region. Spoken guidance requested a step backward when an edge was missing. and four stable observations were required Engineers later confirmed the suggested order. clear the panels, replace the bearing. then tighten the connector. The six-minute repair caused no critical interruption. Trustworthy automation must expose uncertainty and leave final responsibility with the human operator.

Field Evaluation of Wearable Translation Glasses A wearable translation system is most useful when it behaves like an ordinary tool rather than a laboratory demonstration The user should be able to face a printed page. pause briefly, and hear a clear rendering without holding a telephone or searching through menus In the prototype described here, a small camera is mounted near eye level and connected to a compact computer. Video is sent over a local link to a processing workstation. where text detection, optical character recognition, language translation. and speech synthesis are performed The complete pipeline operates without a cloud service This arrangement protects sensitive documents, avoids delays caused by an unstable internet connection, and allows every software component to be measured independently Image acquisition is the first major difficulty A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view The page may be tiited. partly shadowed. or closer at the top than at the bottom Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it. It locates groups of text. estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image, and checks that a safe border remains around the detected region. Sharpness is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion, because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lines remain soft A frame is accepted only after several consecutive observations agree Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or right, hold still. or improve the lighting After capture, the image is converted to grayscale and corrected only when the correction improves measured recognition. Excessive sharpening can create bright halos around letters. while aggressive thresholding can erase punctuation and thin strokes. For that reason. several preprocessing alternatives are tested on the same stored photographs The comparison includes raw grayscale. local contrast enhancement, mild gamma correction edge-preserving filtering. and adaptive binarization Each alternative is evaluated using character count, recognition confidence, focus statistics. and processing time Ground-truth text is retained for important experiments so that character error rate and word error rate can be calculated instead of relying on confidence alone The recognition stage preserves reading order and line positions Translation proceeds paragraph by paragraph. while a short tone identifies each new region Simple controls let the listener repeat the current section or move forward and backward

Field Evaluation of Wearable Translation Glasses A wearable translation system is most useful when it behaves like an ordinary tool rather than a laboratory demonstration. The user should be able to face a printed page, pause briefly, and hear a clear rendering without holding a telephone or searching through menus. In the prototype described here, a small camera is mounted near eye level and connected to a compact computer Video is sent over a local link to a processing workstation, where text detection optical character recognition, language translation and speech synthesis are performed. The complete pipeline operates without a cloud service This arrangement protects sensitive documents. avoids delays caused by an unstable internet connection and allows every software component to be measured independently Image acquisition is the first major difficulty A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view The page may be tilted. partly shadowed. or closer at the top than at the bottom Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it it locates groups of text, estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image, and checks that a safe border remains around the detected region. Sharpness is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion, because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lines remain soft A frame is accepted enly after several consecutive observations agree Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or right, hold still. or improve the lighting After capture. the image is converted to grayscale and corrected only when the correction improves measured recognition. Excessive sharpening can create bright halos around letters, while aggressive threshoiding can erase punctuation and thin strokes. For that reason, several preprocessing alternatives are tested on the same stored photographs The comparison includes raw grayscale, local contrast enhancement mild gamma correction, edge-preserving fiitering. and adaptive binarization. Each alternative is evaluated using character count. recognition confidence. focus statistics, and processing time. Ground-truth text is retained for important experiments so that character error rate and word error rate can be calculated instead of relying on confidence alone The recognition stage preserves reading order and line positions Translation proceeds paragraph by paragraph. while a short tone identifies each new region. Simple controls let the listener repeat the current section or move forward and backward

EXTRACTED TEXT:
偏远地区混合能源站的自主监测与维护 一座高原试验站依靠太阳能阵列、锂电池和小型柴油发电机供 电。微电网需要持续支持诊所、无线电中继、气象设备和安全照 明。冬季道路可能封闭数日，网络也不稳定，因此本地控制器每 二百毫秒采集电压、电流、温度与振动数据，并在能源不足时优 先保障医疗和通信负载。完整记录保存在站内，只有压缩后的状 态摘要会在链路恢复时发送到控制中心。 二〇二五年十月十八日，一场沙尘风暴使太阳能输出在十五分 钟内下降百分之三十四，电池柜温度升高八摄氏度，逆变器风扇 还出现异常低频振动。控制器没有关闭整座电站，而是断开非必 要加热装置、降低部分照明功率并启动备用发电机。诊断模块随 后提出三个可能原因：太阳能板被碎屑遮挡、风扇轴承磨损，以 及电池连接器的接触电阻上升。 风暴减弱后，技术员用头戴式摄像设备读取铭牌、序列号和报 警代码，本地处理单元再与离线维护手册进行比对。由于资料涉 及关键基础设施，图像没有上传云端。采集程序先确认整个标签 位于安全边界内，并分别检查全图和上部区域的清晰度；若画面 被裁切，耳机会提示向左、向右或向后移动。目标只有连续四帧 稳定且文字足够清楚时才会保存。第二天的日志表明，自动排序 与人工判断一致：先清理面板，再更换风扇轴承，最后紧固电池 端子。处置用了六分钟，关键服务未中断。这说明可靠的自动化 必须解释判断、承认不确定性，并把最终决定留给人。
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
TRANSLATED TEXT:
Autonomous monitoring and maintenance of remote hybrid power stations A highland test station relies on solar arrays, lithium batteries and small diesel generators for power. Micro-grids need to continue to support clinics, radio relay, weather equipment and safety lighting. Roads can be closed for days in winter, and the network is unstable, so local controllers collect voltage, current, temperature and vibration data every 200 milliseconds, and optimally protect medical and communications loads when energy is scarce. The complete record is stored on the station, and only the compressed state summary is sent to the control center when the link is restored. On October 18, 2005, a sandstorm caused the solar output to drop 34 percent in fifteen minutes, the temperature of the battery cabinet to rise eight degrees Celsius, and the inverter fan to vibrate at an abnormally low frequency. The controller does not shut down the entire power station, but disconnects the necessary heating devices, reduces the power of some lighting and starts the backup generator. Diagnostic modules suggested three possible causes: solar panels were shrouded in debris, fan bearings wore out, and the contact resistance of the battery connector rose. After the storm weakened, technicians used head-mounted cameras to read the insignia, serial numbers and alarm codes, and the local processing unit was compared to the offline maintenance manual. The images are not uploaded to the cloud because the data is about critical infrastructure. The extractor first confirms that the entire label is within the safe boundary and checks the clarity of the whole image and the upper region separately; if the image is cropped, the earpiece is prompted to move left, right or backwards. The target is saved only when the sequence is stable and the text is clear enough. The next day's log shows that the automatic sorting is consistent with the artificial judgment: first the panel is cleaned, then the fan bearing is replaced, and finally the battery is tightened. The disposal took six minutes and critical services were not interrupted. This shows that reliable automation must explain judgments, acknowledge uncertainty, and leave the final decision to humans.

PARAGRAPH 1 | BBOX=(768, 0, 1873, 840) | CONFIDENCE=0.998
SOURCE     : 偏远地区混合能源站的自主监测与维护 一座高原试验站依靠太阳能阵列、锂电池和小型柴油发电机供 电。微电网需要持续支持诊所、无线电中继、气象设备和安全照 明。冬季道路可能封闭数日，网络也不稳定，因此本地控制器每 二百毫秒采集电压、电流、温度与振动数据，并在能源不足时优 先保障医疗和通信负载。完整记录保存在站内，只有压缩后的状 态摘要会在链路恢复时发送到控制中心。 二〇二五年十月十八日，一场沙尘风暴使太阳能输出在十五分 钟内下降百分之三十四，电池柜温度升高八摄氏度，逆变器风扇 还出现异常低频振动。控制器没有关闭整座电站，而是断开非必 要加热装置、降低部分照明功率并启动备用发电机。诊断模块随 后提出三个可能原因：太阳能板被碎屑遮挡、风扇轴承磨损，以 及电池连接器的接触电阻上升。 风暴减弱后，技术员用头戴式摄像设备读取铭牌、序列号和报 警代码，本地处理单元再与离线维护手册进行比对。由于资料涉 及关键基础设施，图像没有上传云端。采集程序先确认整个标签 位于安全边界内，并分别检查全图和上部区域的清晰度；若画面 被裁切，耳机会提示向左、向右或向后移动。目标只有连续四帧 稳定且文字足够清楚时才会保存。第二天的日志表明，自动排序 与人工判断一致：先清理面板，再更换风扇轴承，最后紧固电池 端子。处置用了六分钟，关键服务未中断。这说明可靠的自动化 必须解释判断、承认不确定性，并把最终决定留给人。
TRANSLATED : Autonomous monitoring and maintenance of remote hybrid power stations A highland test station relies on solar arrays, lithium batteries and small diesel generators for power. Micro-grids need to continue to support clinics, radio relay, weather equipment and safety lighting. Roads can be closed for days in winter, and the network is unstable, so local controllers collect voltage, current, temperature and vibration data every 200 milliseconds, and optimally protect medical and communications loads when energy is scarce. The complete record is stored on the station, and only the compressed state summary is sent to the control center when the link is restored. On October 18, 2005, a sandstorm caused the solar output to drop 34 percent in fifteen minutes, the temperature of the battery cabinet to rise eight degrees Celsius, and the inverter fan to vibrate at an abnormally low frequency. The controller does not shut down the entire power station, but disconnects the necessary heating devices, reduces the power of some lighting and starts the backup generator. Diagnostic modules suggested three possible causes: solar panels were shrouded in debris, fan bearings wore out, and the contact resistance of the battery connector rose. After the storm weakened, technicians used head-mounted cameras to read the insignia, serial numbers and alarm codes, and the local processing unit was compared to the offline maintenance manual. The images are not uploaded to the cloud because the data is about critical infrastructure. The extractor first confirms that the entire label is within the safe boundary and checks the clarity of the whole image and the upper region separately; if the image is cropped, the earpiece is prompted to move left, right or backwards. The target is saved only when the sequence is stable and the text is clear enough. The next day's log shows that the automatic sorting is consistent with the artificial judgment: first the panel is cleaned, then the fan bearing is replaced, and finally the battery is tightened. The disposal took six minutes and critical services were not interrupted. This shows that reliable automation must explain judgments, acknowledge uncertainty, and leave the final decision to humans.
SPOKEN     : Autonomous monitoring and maintenance of remote hybrid power stations A highland test station relies on solar arrays, lithium batteries and small diesel generators for power. EXTRACTED TEXT:
Autonomous Monitoring of a Remote Hybrid-Energy Station An isolated plateau station powers a medical clinic, radio repeater, weather instruments, and emergency lighting. Its microgrid combines solar panels, lithium batteries, and a compact diesel generator. Because winter roads may remain closed for days, a local controller samples voltage, current, temperature, and vibration every 200 milliseconds. Detailed records stay on site, while compressed summaries are transmitted whenever the link becomes available. Medical and communications loads always receive priority. On 18 October 2025, a dust storm reduced solar generation by 34 percent in fifteen minutes. Battery-cabinet temperature increased by 8 °C, and the inverter fan developed an unusual low-frequency vibration. Rather than shut down the station, the controller disconnected secondary heaters, reduced selected lighting, and started the backup generator. Diagnostic software separated the incident into three likely faults: debris on the solar array. wear in a fan bearing. and rising contact resistance at a battery connector. After the storm, a head-mounted camera read equipment labels and alarm codes, which a local processor compared with an offline manual. Sensitive images were not uploaded to the cloud. The capture program required the complete label to remain inside a safe border and checked sharpness across the full frame and its upper region. Spoken guidance requested a step backward when an edge was missing, and four stable observations were required. Engineers later confirmed the suggested order: clear the panels, replace the bearing. then tighten the connector. The six-minute repair caused no critical interruption. Trustworthy automation must expose uncertainty and leave final responsibility with the human operator.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

PARAGRAPHS  : 1

EXTRACTED TEXT:
Offline Inspection at a Remote Energy Facility A maintenance team operates a hybrid-energy station on a dry plateau several hours from the nearest town. The station supplies a medical room. a radio repeater. weather instruments, refrigeration. and emergency lighting. Solar panels provide most of the daily energy. lithium batteries cover the evening demand, and a compact diesel generator is reserved for long storms Because winter roads can remain closed for days, the control cabinet stores detailed measurements locally Voltage. current, temperature, fan speed, and vibration are sampled every two hundred milliseconds. Only compressed summaries are transmitted when the radio link becomes available. and medical and communications loads always receive priority During a dust storm on 18 October 2025, solar output fell by thirty-four percent in fifteen minutes Battery-cabinet temperature rose by eight degrees Celsius. and the inverter fan developed an unusual low- frequency vibration. The controller did not shut down the entire station It disconnected secondary heaters, reduced selected lighting. started the backup generator, and issued a maintenance warning Diagnostic software identified three plausible faults debris covering part of the solar array. wear in a fan bearing. and increasing contact resistance at a battery connector These possibilities were ranked, but none was presented as certain because the measurements could be explained by more than one physical condition When the storm weakened, a technician approached the cabinet while wearing a head-mounted camera and an earpiece Equipment labels contained model numbers, safety notices, alarm codes, and short repair instructions in several languages. The local translation system first checked whether the complete label was visible. It rejected frames with a missing edge, heavy glare, severe perspective distortion, or poor sharpness in the upper region. Four stable frames were required before a photograph was stored If the target was too close, the earpiece asked the technician to step backward. If the label was off centre, a simple left or right instruction was played. These cues were deliberately brief so they would not compete with environmental sounds or safety communication. Accepted images were processed on a workstation inside the service vehicle Text boxes were arranged in reading order and grouped into paragraphs The offline translation model passed one region at a time to the speech engine, and a brief tone marked every transition The technician could repeat. pause, or skip without removing gloves, while sensitive photographs and serial numbers remained on the local system
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Current, temperature, fan speed, and vibration are sampled every two hundred milliseconds. Only compressed increasing summaries are transmitted when the radio link becomes available and medical and backup loads always receive emergency lighting. During a dust storm on October 18, 2025, solar panel output fell by thirty-four percent in fifteen minutes. EXTRACTED TEXT:
Field Evaluation of Wearable Translation Glasses A wearable translation system is most useful when it behaves like an ordinary tool rather than a laboratory demonstration The user should be able to face a printed page, pause briefly, and hear a clear rendering without holding a telephone or searching through menus. In the prototype described here, a small camera is mounted near eye level and connected to a compact computer. Video is sent over a local link to a processing workstation. where text detection, optical character recognition, language translation, and speech synthesis are performed. The complete pipeline operates without a cloud service This arrangement protects sensitive documents, avoids delays caused by an unstable internet connection, and allows every software component to be measured independently Image acquisition is the first major difficulty A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view The page may be tilted, partly shadowed. or closer at the top than at the bottom Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it. It locates groups of text, estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image, and checks that a safe border remains around the detected region. Sharpness is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion, because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lines remain soft A frame is accepted only after several consecutive observations agree Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or right, hold still, or improve the lighting After capture, the image is converted to grayscale and corrected only when the correction improves measured recognition. Excessive sharpening can create bright halos around letters, while aggressive thresholding can erase punctuation and thin strokes. For that reason. several preprocessing alternatives are tested on the same stored photographs The comparison includes raw grayscale, local contrast enhancement, mild gamma correction. edge-preserving filtering. and adaptive binarization Each alternative is evaluated using character count, recognition confidence. focus statistics, and processing time. Ground-truth text is retained for important experiments so that character error rate and word error rate can be calculated instead of relying on confidence alone. The recognition stage preserves reading order and line positions Translation proceeds paragraph by paragraph, while a short tone identifies each new region Simple controls let the listener repeat the current section or move forward and backward.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The local translation system first checked whether the complete label was visible. It rejected frames with a missing edge. heavy glare, severe perspective distortion, or poor sharpness in the upper region. Four stable frames were required before a photograph was stored. If the target was too close, the earpiece asked the technician to step backward. if the label was off centre a simple left or nght instruction was played. These cues were deliberately brief so they would not compete with environmental sounds or safety communication Accepted images were processed on a workstation inside the service

EXTRACTED TEXT:
Designing Reliable Automatic Page Capture Automatic page capture seems simple until the camera is worn on the head. The user cannot continuously inspect a preview. and small movements alter framing. focus, and perspective A page that looks acceptable from a distance may have its first lines outside the image or noticeably softer than the lower half. Indoor lighting adds reflections, while daylight produces deep shadows near the page edge The capture system must therefore decide when a frame is useful and communicate corrections through sound. It should not save the first image containing text, because detection often begins while the wearer is still moving into position The proposed gate combines geometry. focus, exposure, and temporal stability. Text boxes are detected in each video frame and merged into a candidate region. The outer region must remain inside a safety margin so no line is cropped. Its width and height must also fall within practical limits: a tiny region provides too few pixels per character. but a region touching the image boundary probably indicates that part of the page is missing. Focus is estimated from Laplacian variance over the full grayscale frame A second measurement covers the upper thirty percent, where slanted paper is commonly out of focus. A capture is rejected when the upper score is much lower than the full-frame score, even if the overall number appears satisfactory. One sharp frame is not sufficient evidence. The position and size of the text region must remain stable across four consecutive observations. With the selected video interval, this adds roughly eight tenths of a second after the page first appears ready. The delay is short for the wearer but long enough for hand and head motion to settle. Exposure changes are monitored during the same period. If brightness is still drifting, the counter returns to zero. When the page is too large. spoken guidance asks the user to step back. Missing space on one side produces a left or right cue, and persistent softness produces a request to hold still or adjust distance.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Creates a serious usabllity problem. The listener hears the meaning but cannot tell which original line or paragraph is currently being spoken. This becomes especially confusing on technical documents containing warnings, numbered procedures. labels. and tables. A wearable translator should preserve the connection between physical text and audio. The processing pipeline therefore retains the coordinates returned by optical character recognition and groups nearby lines into meaningful regions. Each region becomes a separate translation unit instead of sending the entire page to the language model at once Reading order is determined from position, alignment, and spacing. Lines that share a similar left edge and remain within a reasonable vertical distance are combined. Large gaps, headings, bullet points, and changes in indentation begin new groups. The original coordinates remain attached to every translated sentence During development, the selected paragraph is surrounded by a coloured box in the preview. In the wearable version, a short tone and a spoken paragraph number announce the same transition. The user can move forward. go back, repeat, pause, or stop with a small physical control or a limited voice command set. Speech is generated only after a paragraph passes basic checks. Empty results and very low recognition confidence request another image Extremely long regions are divided at sentence boundaries, while short neighbouring lines may be joined so the voice does not pause after every label fragment. Numbers. units. dates, and warning symbols receive special attention because a fluent sentence can still be dangerous when one measurement is wrong. The interface can optionally read the source paragraph first and the translated paragraph second. This slower mode helps during evaluation and allows bilingual users to notice recognition mistakes before acting on the result.

EXTRACTED TEXT:
EoitorAdd-ins Field Evaluation of Wearable Translation Glasses A wearable translation system is most useful when it behaves like an ordinary tool rather than a laboratory demonstration. The user should be able to face a printed page, pause briefly, and hear a clear rendering without holding a telephone or searching through menus. In the prototype described here, a small camera is mounted near eye level and connected to a compact computer. Video is sent over a local link to a processing workstation, where text detection, optical character recognition, language translation, and speech synthesis are performed. The complete pipeline operates without a cloud service. This arrangement protects sensitive documents, avoids delays caused by an unstable internet connection, and allows every software component to be measured independently. Image acquisition is the first major difficulty. A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view. The page may be tilted, partly shadowed, or closer at the top than at the bottom. Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur. The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it. It locates groups of text, estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image, and checks that a safe border remains around the detected reglon. Sharpness Is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion, because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lilnes remaln soft. A frame is accepted only after several consecutive observatlons agree. Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or right, hold still, or improve the lighting. yroow Aesoaly Good to go
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
CONSERVATIVELY CORRECTED TEXT:
EoitorAdd-ins Field Evaluation of Wearable Translation Glasses A wearable translation system is most useful when it behaves like an ordinary tool rather than a laboratory demonstration. The user should be able to face a printed page, pause briefly, and hear a clear rendering without holding a telephone or searching through menus. In the prototype described here, a small camera is mounted near eye level and connected to a compact computer. Video is sent over a local link to a processing workstation, where text detection, optical character recognition, language translation, and speech synthesis are performed. The complete pipeline operates without a cloud service. This arrangement protects sensitive documents, avoids delays caused by an unstable internet connection, and allows every software component to be measured independently. Image acquisition is the first major difficulty. A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view. The page may be tilted, partly shadowed, or closer at the top than at the bottom. Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur. The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it. It locates groups of text, estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image, and checks that a safe border remains around the detected region. Sharpness Is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion, because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lilnes remain soft. A frame is accepted only after several consecutive observations agree. Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or right, hold still, or improve the lighting. yroow Aesoaly Good to go

Field Evaluation of Wearable Translation Glasses A wearable translation system is most useful when it behaves like an ordinary tool rather than a laboratory demonstration. The user should be able to face a printed page. pause briefly, and hear a clear rendering without holding a telephone or searching through menus. In the prototype described here, a small camera is mounted near eye level and connected to a compact computer Video is sent over a local link to a processing workstation, where text detection, optical character recognition, language translation. and speech synthesis are performed. The complete pipeline operates without a cloud service. This arrangement protects sensitive documents, avoids delays caused by an unstable internet connection. and allows every software component to be measured independently Image acquisition is the first major difficulty A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view The page may be tilted. partly shadowed, or closer at the top than at the bottom Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it It locates groups of text, estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image, and checks that a safe border remains around the detected region Sharpness is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion, because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lines remain soft. A frame is accepted only after several consecutive observations agree Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or right, hold still, or improve the lighting After capture, the image is converted to grayscale and corrected only when the correction improves measured recognition Excessive sharpening can create bright halos around letters, while aggressive thresholding can erase punctuation and thin strokes For that reason. several preprocessing alternatives are tested on the same stored photographs The comparison includes raw grayscale, local contrast enhancement, mild gamma correction, edge-preserving filtering. and adaptive binarization. Each alternative is evaluated using character count recognition confidence, focus statistics, and processing time Ground-truth text is retained for important experiments so that character error rate and word error rate can be calculated instead of relying on confidence alone The recognition stage preserves reading order and line positions. Translation proceeds paragraph by paragraph, while a short tone identifies each new region. Simple controls let the listener repeat the

EXTRACTED TEXT:
Field Evaluation of Wearable Translation Glasses A wearable translation system is most useful when it behaves like an ordinary tool rather than a laboratory demonstration The user should be able to face a printed page. pause briefly. and hear a clear rendering without holding a telephone or searching through menus. In the prototype described here, a small camera is mounted near eye level and connected to a compact computer Video is sent over a local link to a processing workstation, where text detection, optical character recognition, language translation. and speech synthesis are performed. The complete pipeline operates without a cloud service This arrangement protects sensitive documents, avoids delays caused by an unstable internet connection and allows every software component to be measured independently Image acquisition is the first major difficulty. A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view The page may be tilted, partly shadowed, or closer at the top than at the bottom Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it. It locates groups of text. estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image, and checks that a safe border remains around the detected region. Sharpness is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion, because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lines remain soft A frame is accepted only after several consecutive observations agree Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or right, hold still. or improve the lighting After capture, the image is converted to grayscale and corrected only when the correction improves measured recognition Excessive sharpening can create bright halos around letters, while aggressive thresholding can erase punctuation and thin strokes For that reason several preprocessing alternatives are tested on the same stored photographs. The comparison includes raw grayscale, local contrast enhancement, mild gamma correction, edge-preserving filtering, and adaptive binarization. Each alternative is evaluated using character count, recognition confidence, focus statistics, and processing time. Ground-truth text is retained for important experiments so that character error rate and word error rate can be calculated instead of relying on confidence alone
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

EXTRACTED TEXT:
A wearable translation system is most usefui when it behaves like an ordinary tool rather than a laboratory demonatration The user should be able to face a printed page. pause briefly. and hear a clear rendering without holding a telephone or searching through menus. In the prototype described here a small camera is mounted near eye level and connected to a compact computer Video is sent over a local link to a processing workstation where text detection, optical character recognition, language translation, and speech synthesis are performed The complete pipeline operates without a cloud service This arrangement protects sensitive documents, avoids delays caused by an unstable internet connection and allows every software component to be measured independently Image acquisition is the first major difficulty A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view. The page may be tilted. partly shadowed, or closer at the top tham at the bottom Motion from breathing and head moverment also creates blur The capture controller therefore examines every incoming ftame before saving it. It locates groups of text, estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image, and checks that a safe border remains around the detected region. Sharpness is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion, because a sianted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lines remain soft. A frame is accepted only after several consecutive observations agree. Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or right, hold still. or improve the lighting After capture, the image is converted to grayscale and corrected only when the correction improves measured recognition. Excessive sharpening can create bright halos around letters, while aggressive thresholding can erase punctuation and thin strokes For that reason. several preprocessing alternatives are tested on the same stored photographs. The comparison includes raw grayscale. local contrast enhancement. mild gamma correction, edge-preserving filtering. and adaptive binarization Each alternative is evaluated using character count. recognition confidence. focus statistics, and processing time. Ground-truth text is retained for important experiments so that character error rate and word error rate can be calculated instead of relying on confidence alone

EXTRACTED TEXT:
Field Evaluation of Wearable Translation Glasses A wearable translation system is most useful when it behaves like an ordinary tool rather than a laboratory demonstration. The user should be able to face a printed page. pause briefly. and hear a clear rendering without holding a telephone or searching through menus. In the prototype described here, a small camera is mounted near eye level and connected to a compact computer Video is sent over a local link to a processing workstation, where text detection, optical character recognition, language translation and speech synthesis are performed. The complete pipeline operates without a cloud service This arrangement protects sensitive documents avoids delays caused by an unstable internet connection. and allows every software component to be measured independently Image acquisition is the first major difficulty A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view. The page may be tilted. partly shadowed. or closer at the top than at the bottom Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it It locates groups of text. estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image, and checks that a safe border remains around the detected region Sharpness is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion. because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lines remain soft A frame is accepted only after several consecutive observations agree Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or right, hold still. or improve the lighting After capture the image is converted to grayscale and corrected only when the correction improves measured recognition Excessive sharpening can create bright halos around letters, while aggressive thresholding can erase punctuation and thin strokes. For that reason, several preprocessing alternatives are tested on the same stored pihotographs. The comparison includes raw grayscale. local contrast enhancement, mild gamma correction, edge-preserving filtering. and adaptive binarization. Each alternative is evaluated using character count. recognition confidence, focus statistics, and processing time Ground-truth text is retained for important experiments so that character error rate and word error rate can be calculated instead of relying on confidence alone

EXTRACTED TEXT:
Offline Inspection at a Remote Energy Facility A maintenance team operates a hybrid-energy station on a dry plateau 1 several hours from the nearest town. The station supplies a medical room, a radio repeater. weather instruments. refrigeration. and emergency lighting Solar panels provide most of the daily energy. lithium batteries cover the evening demand. and a compact diesel generator is reserved for long storms Because winter roads can remain closed for days, the control cabinet stores detailed measurements locally Voltage. current temperature. fan speed. and vibration are sampled every two hundred milliseconds Only compressed summaries are transmitted when the radio link becomes available, and medical and communications loads always receive priority During a dust storm on 18 October 2025, solar output fell by thirty-four percent in fifteen minutes Battery-cabinet temperature rose by eight degrees Celsius. and the inverter fan developed an unusual low- frequency vibration The controller did not shut down the entire station. It disconnected secondary heaters. reduced selected lighting. started the backup generator. and issued a maintenance warning Diagnostic software identified three plausible faults debris covering part of the solar array. wear in a fan bearing. and increasing contact resistance at a battery connector These possibilites were ranked but none was more than one physical condition When the storm weakened. a technician approached the cabinet while wearing a head-mounted camera and an earpiece Equipment labels contained model numbers. safety notices. alarm codes, and short repair instructions in several languages. The local translation system first checked whether the complete label was visible. it rejected frames with a missing edge. heavy glare. severe perspective distortion or poor sharpness in the upper region Four stable frames were required before a photograph was stored If the target was too close. the earpiece asked the technician to step backward. If the label was off centre. a simple left or right instruction was played. These cues were deliberately brief so they would not compete with environmental sounds or safety communication Accepted images were processed on a workstation inside the service vehicle Text boxes were arranged in reading order and grouped into paragraphs. The offline translation model passed one region at a time to the speech engine, and a brief tone marked every transition

Offline Inspection at a Remote Energy Facility A maintenance team operates a hybrid-energy station on a dry plateau several hours from the nearest town The station supplies a medical room a radio repeater, weather instruments. refrigeration. and emergency lighting. Solar panels provide most of the daily energy. lithium batteries cover the evening demand, and a compact diesel generator is reserved for long storms. Because winter roads can remain closed for days. the control cabinet stores detailed measurements locally Voltage. current temperature, fan speed. and vibration are sampled every two hundred milliseconds Only compressed summaries are transmitted when the radio link becomes available, and medical and communications loads always receive priority During a dust storm on 18 October 2025. solar output fell by thirty-four percent in fifteen minutes Battery-cabinet temperature rose by eight degrees Celsius. and the inverter fan developed an unusual low- frequency vibration The controller did not shut down the entire station It disconnected secondary heaters, reduced selected lighting, started the backup generator. and issued a maintenance warning Diagnostic software identified three plausible faults debris covering part of the solar array. wear in a fan bearing. and increasing contact resistance at a battery connector These possibilities were ranked, but none was presented as certain because the measurements could be explained by more than one physical condition When the storm weakened, a technician approached the cabinet while wearing a head-mounted camera and an earpiece Equipment labels contained model numbers, safety notices, alarm codes, and short repair instructions in several languages. The local translation system first checked whether the complete label was visible. It rejected frames with a missing edge, heavy glare, severe perspective distortion, or poor sharpness in the upper region Four stable frames were required before a photograph was stored If the target was too close, the earpiece asked the technician to step backward If the label was off centre, a simple left or right instruction was played These cues were deliberately brief so they would not compete with environmental sounds or safety communication Accepted images were processed on a workstation inside the service vehicle. Text boxes were arranged in reading order and grouped into paragraphs. The offline translation model passed one region at a time to the speech engine and a brief tone

TIMESTAMP   : 2026-07-16 14:18:38
CODE VERSION: pipeline_cli_box3d1.py
RUN NUMBER  : 12
IMAGE FILE  : capture_cli_012_20260716_141836.jpg
PARAGRAPHS  : 2
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
EXTRACTED TEXT:
TERALEE Designing Reliable Automatic Page Capture Automatic page capture seems simple until the camera is worn on the head. The user cannot continuously inspect a preview. and small movements alter framing. focus, and perspective. A page that looks acceptable from a distance may have its first lines outside the image or noticeably softer than the lower half. Indoor lighting adds reflections, while daylight produces deep shadows near the page edge. The capture system must therefore decide when a frame is useful and communicate corrections through sound. It should not save the first image containing text, because detection often begins while the wearer is still moving into position The proposed gate combines geometry. focus, exposure, and temporal stability Text boxes are detected in each video frame and merged into a candidate region. The outer region must remain inside a safety margin so no line is cropped. Its width and height must also fall within practical limits: a tiny region provides too few pixels per character, but a region touching the image boundary probably indicates that part of the page is missing. Focus is estimated from Laplacian variance over the full grayscale frame. A second measurement covers the upper thirty percent, where slanted paper is commoniy out of focus. A capture is rejected when the upper score is much lower than the full-frame score, even if the overall number appears satisfactory One sharp frame is not sufficient evidence. The position and size of the text region must remain stable across four consecutive obseryations. With the selected video interval, this adds roughly eight tanths of a second after the page first appears ready. The delay is short for the wearer but long enough for hand and head motion to settle. Exposure changes are monitored during the same period. if brightness is still drifting. the counter returns to zero. When the page is too large. spoken guidance asks the user to step back. Missing space on one side produces a left or right cue. and persistent softness produces a request to hold still or adjust distance
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

EXTRACTED TEXT:
Designing Reliable Automatic Page Capture Automatic page capture seems simple until the camera is worn on the head. The user cannot continuously inspect a preview. and small movements alter framing. focus, and perspective. A page that looks acceptable from a distance may have its first lines outside the image or noticeably softer than the lower half Indoor lighting adds reflections, while daylight produces deep shadows near the page edge The capture system must therefore decide when a frame is useful and communicate corrections through sound. It should not save the first image containing text. because detection often begins while the wearer is still moving into position The proposed gate combines geometry, focus, exposure, and temporal stability. Text boxes are detected in each video frame and merged into a candidate region. The outer region must remain inside a safety margin so no line is cropped. Its width and height must also fall within practical limits: a tiny region provides too few pixels per character, but a region touching the image boundary probably indicates that part of the page is missing. Focus is estimated from Laplacian variance over the full grayscale frame. A second measurement covers the upper thirty percent, where slanted paper is commonly out of focus. A capture is rejected when the upper score is much lower than the full-frame score, even if the overall number appears satisfactory. One sharp frame is not sufficient evidence. The position and size of the text region must remain stable across four consecutive observations. With the selected video interval, this adds roughly eight tenths of a second after the page first appears ready. The delay is short for the wearer but long enough for hand and head motion to settle. Exposure changes are monitored during the same period If brightness is still drifting, the counter returns to zero When the page is too large, spoken guidance asks the user to step back. Missing space on one side produces a left or right cue, and persistent softness produces a request to hold still or adjust distance.

Designing Reliable Automatic Page Capture Automatic page capture seems simple until the camera is worn on the head The user cannot continuously inspect a preview. and small movements alter framing, focus, and perspective. A page that looks acceptable from a distance may have its first lines outside the image or noticeably softer than the lower half. Indoor lighting adds reflections, while daylight produces deep shadows near the page edge. The capture system must therefore decide when a frame is useful and communicate corrections through sound. It should not save the first image containing text, because detection often begins while the wearer is still moving into position The proposed gate combines geometry, focus, exposure, and temporal stability Text boxes are detected in each video frame and merged into a candidate region. The outer region must remain inside a safety margin so no line is cropped. Its width and height must also fall within practical limits: a tiny region provides too few pixels per character, but a region touching the image boundary probably indicates that part of the page is missing Focus is  estimated from Laplacian variance over the full grayscale frame A second measurement covers the upper thirty percent. where slanted paper is commonly out of focus. A capture is rejected when the upper score is much lower than the full-frame score, even if the overall number appears satisfactory One sharp frame is not sufficient evidence. The position and size of the text region must remain stable across four consecutive observations With the selected video interval, this adds roughly eight tenths of a second after the page first appears ready. The delay is short for the wearer but long enough for hand and head motion to settle. Exposure changes are monitored during the same period. If brightness is still drifting. the counter returns to zero When the page is too large, spoken guidance asks the user to step back. Missing space on one side produces a left or right cue, and persistent softness produces a request to hold still or adjust distance.

SOURCE     : Designing Reliable Automatic Page Capture Automatic page capture seems simple until the camera is worn on the head The user cannot continuously inspect a preview. and small movements alter framing, focus, and perspective. A page that looks acceptable from a distance may have its first lines outside the image or noticeably softer than the lower half. Indoor lighting adds reflections, while daylight produces deep shadows near the page edge. The capture system must therefore decide when a frame is useful and communicate corrections through sound. It should not save the first image containing text, because detection often begins while the wearer is still moving into position The proposed gate combines geometry, focus, exposure, and temporal stability Text boxes are detected in each video frame and merged into a candidate region. The outer region must remain inside a safety margin so no line is cropped. Its width and height must also fall within practical limits: a tiny region provides too few pixels per character, but a region touching the image boundary probably indicates that part of the page is missing Focus is  estimated from Laplacian variance over the full grayscale frame A second measurement covers the upper thirty percent. where slanted paper is commonly out of focus. A capture is rejected when the upper score is much lower than the full-frame score, even if the overall number appears satisfactory One sharp frame is not sufficient evidence. The position and size of the text region must remain stable across four consecutive observations With the selected video interval, this adds roughly eight tenths of a second after the page first appears ready. The delay is short for the wearer but long enough for hand and head motion to settle. Exposure changes are monitored during the same period. If brightness is still drifting. the counter returns to zero When the page is too large, spoken guidance asks the user to step back. Missing space on one side produces a left or right cue, and persistent softness produces a request to hold still or adjust distance.
SPOKEN     : Designing Reliable Automatic Page Capture Automatic page capture seems simple until the camera is worn on the head The user cannot continuously inspect a preview. and small movements alter framing, focus, and perspective. IMAGE FILE  : capture_cli_015_20260716_141947.jpg
PARAGRAPHS  : 1

EXTRACTED TEXT:
Reading a complete translated page as uninterrupted speech creates a serious usability problem. The listener hears the meaning but cannot tell which original line or paragraph is currently being spoken This becomes especially confusing on technical documents containing warnings, numbered procedures. labels, and tables. A wearable translator should preserve the connection between physical text and audio. The processing pipeline therefore retains the coordinates returned by optical character recognition and groups nearby lines into meaningful regions. Each region becomes a separate translation unit instead of sending the entire page to the language model at once. Reading order is determined from position, alignment, and spacing Lines that share a similar left edge and remain within a reasonable vertical distance are combined Large gaps. headings, bullet points, and changes in indentation begin new groups The original coordinates remain attached to every translatedsentenceDuring development,theselected paragraph is surrounded by a coloured box in the preview In the wearable version, a short tone and a spoken paragraph number announce the same transition. The user can move forward, go back, repeat, pause, or stop with a small physical control or a limited voice command set. Speech is generated only after a paragraph passes basic checks. Empty results and very low recognition confidence request another image. Extremely long regions are divided at sentence boundaries, while short neighbouring lines may be joined so the voice does not pause after every label fragment. Numbers, units, dates, and warning symbols receive special attention because a fluent sentence can still be dangerous when one measurement is wrong. The interface can optionally read the source paragraph first and the translated paragraph second. This slower mode helps during evaluation and allows bilingual users to notice recognition mistakes before acting on the result.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

RUN NUMBER  : 16
IMAGE FILE  : capture_cli_016_20260716_142022.jpg
PARAGRAPHS  : 3
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
EXTRACTED TEXT:
Autonomous Monitoring of a Remote Hybrid-Energy Station An isolated plateau station powers a medical clinic, radio repeater. weather instruments. and emergency lighting Its microgrid combines solar panels, lithium batteries, and a compact diesel generator. Because winter roads may remain closed for days, a local controller samples voltage. current. temperature. and vibration every 200 milliseconds Detailed records stay on site. while compressed summaries are transmitted whenever the link becomes available Medical and communications loads always receive priority. On 18 October 2025. a dust storm reduced solar generation by 34 percent in fifteen minutes. Battery-cabinet temperature increased by 8 °C. and the inverter fan developed an unusual low-frequency vibration. Rather than shut down the station, the controller disconnected secondary heaters, reduced selected lighting. and started the backup generator. Diagnostic software separated the incident into three likely faults: debris on the solar array. wear in a fan bearing, and rising contact resistance at a battery connector After the storm, a head-mounted camera read equipment labels and alarm codes, which a local processor compared with an offline manual. Sensitive images were not uploaded to the cloud. The capture program required the complete label to remain inside a safe border and checked sharpness across the full frame and its upper region. Spoken guidance requested a step backward when an edge was missing, and four stable observations were required Engineers later confirmed the suggested order: clear the panels, replace the bearing, then tighten the connector. The six-minute repair caused no critical interruption Trustworthy automation must expose uncertainty and leave final responsibility with the human operator
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

EXTRACTED TEXT:
withour holding a telephone or searching through menus In the prototype described here, a small camera is mounted near eye level and connected to a compact computer Video is sent over a local link to a processing workstation where text detection, optical character recognition, language translation and speech synthesis are performed The complete pipeline operates without a cloud service This arrangement protects sensitive documents avoids delays caused by an unstable internet connection and allows every software component to be measured independently Image acquisition is the first major difficulty A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera at the bottom Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it it locates groups of text. estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image. and checks that a safe border remains around the detected region Sharpness is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion, because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lines remain soft A frame is accepted only after several consecutive observations agree Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or right, hold still, or improve the lighting After capture, the image is converted to grayscale and corrected only when the correction improves measured recognition Excessive sharpening can create bright halos around letters, while aggressive thresholding can erase punctuation and thin strokes For that reason, several preprocessing alternatives are tested on the same stored photographs The comparison includes raw grayscale, local contrast enhancement, mild gamma correction, edge-preserving filtering, and adaptive binarization Each alternative is evaluated using character count recognition confidence, focus statistics, and processing time Ground-truth text is retained for important experiments so that character error rate and word error rate can be calculated instead of relying on confidence alone

Offline Inspection at a Remote Energy Facility A maintenance team operates a hybrid-energy station on a dry plateau several hours from the nearest town The station supplies a medical room, a radio repeater, weather instruments, refrigeration. and emergency lighting Solar panels provide most of the daily energy. lithium batteries cover the evening demand, and a compact diesel generator is reserved for long storms. Because winter roads can remain closed for days. the control cabinet stores detailed measurements locally Voltage. current, temperature. fan speed, and vibration are sampled every two hundred milliseconds. Only compressed summaries are transmitted when the radio link becomes available, and medical and communications loads always receive priority During a dust storm on 18 October 2025. solar output fell by thirty-four percent in fifteen minutes Battery-cabinet temperature rose by eight degrees Celsius, and the inverter fan developed an unusual low- frequency vibration The controller did not shut down the entire station. It disconnected secondary heaters. reduced selected lighting. started the backup generator, and issued a maintenance warning. Diagnostic software identified three plausible faults: debris covering part of the solar array, wear in a fan bearing. and increasing contact resistance at a battery connector. These possibilities were ranked. but none was presented as certain because the measurements could be explained by more than one physical condition When the storm weakened. a technician approached the cabinet while wearing a head-mounted camera and an earpiece. Equipment labels contained model numbers, safety notices, alarm codes, and short repair instructions in several languages. The local translation system first checked whether the complete label was visible. It rejected frames with a missing edge. heavy glare. severe perspective distortion, or poor sharpness in the upper region. Four stable frames were required before a photograph was stored If the target was too close, the earpiece asked the technician to step backward. If the label was off centre, a simple left or right instruction was played. These cues were deliberately brief so they would not compete with environmental sounds or safety communication Accepted images were processed on a workstation inside the service vehicle. Text boxes were arranged in reading order and grouped into paragraphs. The offline translation model passed one region at a time to the speech engine and a brief tope mas

EXTRACTED TEXT:
偏远地区混合能源站的自主监测与维护 一座高原试验站依靠太阳能阵列、锂电池和小型柴油发电机供电。微电 网需要持续支持诊所、无线电中继、气象设备和安全照明。冬季道路可能 封闭数日，网络也不稳定，因此本地控制器每二百毫秒采集电压、电流、 温度与撮动数据，并在能源不足时优先保障医疗和通信负载。完整记录保 存在站内，只有压缩后的状态摘要会在链路恢复时发送到控制中心。 二〇二五年十月十八日，一场沙尘风暴使太阳能输出在十五分钟内下降 百分之三十四，电池柜温度升高八摄氏度，逆变器风扇还出现异常低频振 动。控制器没有关闭整座电站，而是断开非必要加热装置、降低部分照明 功率并启动备用发电机。诊断模块随后提出三个可能原因：太阳能板被碎 屑遮挡、风扇轴承磨损，以及电池连接器的接触电阻上升。 风暴减弱后，技术员用头戴式摄像设备读取铭牌、序列号和报警代码 本地处理单元再与离线维护手册进行比对。由于资料涉及关键基础设施 图像没有上传云端。采集程序先确认整个标签位于安全边界内，并分别检 查全图和上部区域的清晰度：若画面被裁切，耳机会提示向左、向右或向 后移动。目标只有连续四帧稳定且文字足够清楚时才会保存。第二天的日 志表明，自动排序与人工判断一致：先清理面板，再更换风扇轴承，最后 紧固电池端子。处置用了六分钟，关键服务未中断。这说明可靠的自动化 必须解释判断、承认不确定性，并把最终决定留给人。
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
TRANSLATED TEXT:
Autonomous monitoring and maintenance of hybrid power stations in remote areas A plateau test station relies on solar arrays, lithium batteries and a small diesel generator to power it. Micro-networks need to continue to support clinics, radio relay, weather equipment and safety lighting. Roads may be closed for days in winter, and the network is unstable, so local controllers collect voltage, current, temperature and imaging data every 200 milliseconds, and prioritize medical and communications loads when energy is scarce. Complete logs are stored on the station, and only compressed status summaries are sent to the control center when the link is restored. On October 18, 2005, a dust storm caused solar output to drop by 34 percent in fifteen minutes, the temperature of the battery cabinet rose by eight degrees Celsius, and the inverter fan began to vibrate at an abnormally low frequency. Instead of shutting down the entire power plant, the controller disconnects unnecessary heating devices, lowers partial lighting, power and starts the backup generator. The diagnostic module then suggests three possible causes: solar panel breakage, aluminum shielding, fan bearing wear, and increased contact resistance of the battery connector. After the storm weakened, technicians used head-mounted cameras to read the markings, serial numbers and alarm codes of the local processing unit and compare them with the offline maintenance manual. The images are not uploaded to the cloud because of critical infrastructure. The capture process first confirms that the entire label is within the safe boundary and checks the clarity of the whole image and the upper region separately: if the image is cropped, the earpiece is prompted to move left, right or backwards. The target is saved only when the sequence of four syllables is stable and the text is sufficiently clear. The next day's logs showed that the automatic sorting was consistent with the artificial judgment: first the panel was cleaned, then the fan bearings were replaced, and finally the battery terminals were tightened. The disposal took six minutes and critical services were not interrupted. This shows that reliable automation must interpret judgments, acknowledge uncertainty, and leave the final decision to humans.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

SPOKEN     : Autonomous monitoring and maintenance of hybrid power stations in remote areas

PARAGRAPH 2 | BBOX=(881, 115, 1844, 325) | CONFIDENCE=0.987
SOURCE     : 一座高原试验站依靠太阳能阵列、锂电池和小型柴油发电机供电。微电 网需要持续支持诊所、无线电中继、气象设备和安全照明。冬季道路可能 封闭数日，网络也不稳定，因此本地控制器每二百毫秒采集电压、电流、 温度与撮动数据，并在能源不足时优先保障医疗和通信负载。完整记录保 存在站内，只有压缩后的状态摘要会在链路恢复时发送到控制中心。
TRANSLATED : A plateau test station relies on solar arrays, lithium batteries and a small diesel generator to power it. Micro-networks need to continue to support clinics, radio relay, weather equipment and safety lighting. Roads may be closed for days in winter, and the network is unstable, so local controllers collect voltage, current, temperature and imaging data every 200 milliseconds, and prioritize medical and communications loads when energy is scarce. Complete logs are stored on the station, and only compressed status summaries are sent to the control center when the link is restored.
SPOKEN     : A plateau test station relies on solar arrays, lithium batteries and a small diesel generator to power it. PARAGRAPH 3 | BBOX=(873, 354, 1842, 559) | CONFIDENCE=0.992
SOURCE     : 二〇二五年十月十八日，一场沙尘风暴使太阳能输出在十五分钟内下降 百分之三十四，电池柜温度升高八摄氏度，逆变器风扇还出现异常低频振 动。控制器没有关闭整座电站，而是断开非必要加热装置、降低部分照明 功率并启动备用发电机。诊断模块随后提出三个可能原因：太阳能板被碎 屑遮挡、风扇轴承磨损，以及电池连接器的接触电阻上升。
TRANSLATED : On October 18, 2005, a dust storm caused solar output to drop by 34 percent in fifteen minutes, the temperature of the battery cabinet rose by eight degrees Celsius, and the inverter fan began to vibrate at an abnormally low frequency. Instead of shutting down the entire power plant, the controller disconnects unnecessary heating devices, lowers partial lighting, power and starts the backup generator. The diagnostic module then suggests three possible causes: solar panel breakage, aluminum shielding, fan bearing wear, and increased contact resistance of the battery connector.
SPOKEN     : On October 18, 2005, a dust storm caused solar output to drop by 34 percent in fifteen minutes, the temperature of the battery cabinet rose by eight degrees Celsius, and the inverter fan began to vibrate at an abnormally low frequency. Instead of shutting down the entire power plant, the controller disconnects unnecessary heating devices, lowers partial lighting, power and starts the backup generator. PARAGRAPH 4 | BBOX=(840, 591, 1844, 901) | CONFIDENCE=0.996
SOURCE     : 风暴减弱后，技术员用头戴式摄像设备读取铭牌、序列号和报警代码 本地处理单元再与离线维护手册进行比对。由于资料涉及关键基础设施 图像没有上传云端。采集程序先确认整个标签位于安全边界内，并分别检 查全图和上部区域的清晰度：若画面被裁切，耳机会提示向左、向右或向 后移动。目标只有连续四帧稳定且文字足够清楚时才会保存。第二天的日 志表明，自动排序与人工判断一致：先清理面板，再更换风扇轴承，最后 紧固电池端子。处置用了六分钟，关键服务未中断。这说明可靠的自动化 必须解释判断、承认不确定性，并把最终决定留给人。
TRANSLATED : After the storm weakened, technicians used head-mounted cameras to read the markings, serial numbers and alarm codes of the local processing unit and compare them with the offline maintenance manual. The images are not uploaded to the cloud because of critical infrastructure. The capture process first confirms that the entire label is within the safe boundary and checks the clarity of the whole image and the upper region separately: if the image is cropped, the earpiece is prompted to move left, right or backwards. The target is saved only when the sequence of four syllables is stable and the text is sufficiently clear. The next day's logs showed that the automatic sorting was consistent with the artificial judgment: first the panel was cleaned, then the fan bearings were replaced, and finally the battery terminals were tightened. The disposal took six minutes and critical services were not interrupted. This shows that reliable automation must interpret judgments, acknowledge uncertainty, and leave the final decision to humans.
